Free Talk - Past

World Anecdotes - Hai Ke

▲ Women Cutting Their Hair: Now popular in various countries, both East and West. But the first to initiate it were the women of the Butani tribe in India.

▲ In East Ham, England, a newborn baby was born with a tooth. After three weeks, his parents had it removed.

▲ The bees in Australia are particularly small, about the size of half a fly. And they do not have stingers, making them a unique species.

▲ The machines for making cigarettes in England are constantly being improved. They can now produce 50,000 cigarettes per hour and can immediately pack them into boxes, packing 15,000 cigarettes per hour.

▲ Billericay in Essex, England, is the most hygienic town in the country, with a death rate of less than twelve per thousand people.

▲ Making clay pipes was once a famous German industry, sold all over the world, generating huge profits. Now, the production in England is also booming.

▲ On the Adriatic coast of Europe, there is a town called Corrado. Due to frequent heavy rains, the houses collapsed and the entire town was submerged in mud.

▲ In Illinois, USA, a woman often suffered from typhoid fever. The state government, fearing the spread of her germs, ordered her to live alone in a house, provide her own food, and not have contact with others.

▲ A British explorer discovered idols dating back 6,000 years in the interior of Panama and transported them to London. These idols all wore tall hats.

A Glimpse of Guangzhou - Li Qingduo

Guangdong is the cradle of revolution, occupying an important position historically and geographically. In the past, when Minister Sun Zhe Sheng served as the director of the Guangzhou Municipal Government, he spared no effort in reorganizing the municipal administration, demolishing city walls to build roads, and dedicating himself to construction. Guangzhou was thus able to take on a new look. I have not returned to my ancestral home in Guangdong for nearly a decade. So, in January, I took the time to return south for a visit. Although I only stayed for two weeks, there was much to see in the City of Five Rams that is worth mentioning. I will record them here in a miscellaneous fashion.

▲ Narrow Lanes Become Wide Roads: In recent years, the Guangzhou authorities have actively paved roads throughout the city. Narrow streets have also been gradually demolished and rebuilt into roads, making transportation convenient. The number of cars in the city has increased compared to the past. Small electric ferries have also been installed from Guangzhou City to Henan for crossing the river. This is one of the new constructions in recent years. However, many of the street names in the city, especially those along the new Guanma Road, have been changed. After being away for so long, I often couldn't recognize the roads. There is a sense that the people are the same, but the city is different.

▲ Scenic Yuexiu Mountain: Yuexiu Mountain was originally called Guanyin Mountain, located in the northeast corner of Guangzhou. In the past, when Long Jiguang governed Guangdong, he occupied it as his stronghold, hiding here. He built many fortresses on the mountain, looking down on everything from a commanding height. Now, this mountain has been developed into Yuexiu Park and renovated. The abandoned fortresses have been demolished. Visitors cannot help but feel a sense of the past and present. The Zhenhai Tower stands on the peak of the mountain. In recent years, Mayor Lin Yunge renovated the tower and turned it into a museum. He invited Legislative Yuan President Hu Zhantang and former Executive Yuan President Tan Zu'an to write couplets on it. The tower has five floors. Climbing to the top, one can see for miles and have a panoramic view of the Pearl River.

▲ Eastern Suburb Busy with Officials: The eastern suburb is located east of Guangzhou, facing the Pearl River and backed by Baiyun and Yuexiu Mountains. The scenery is beautiful. Guangdong Provincial Chairman Chen Mingshu, Eighth Route Army Commander Chen Jitang, and Guangdong Finance Director Fan Qiwu all chose to reside here. Every day, the streets are bustling with officials and cars. The military and police provide very tight security. Recently, the Eastern Suburb Model District has been developed. Construction of houses is underway. Gu Xiangqin, the Secretary-General of the National Government, has also purchased a house in the district, planning to retire here in the future. Although Guangzhou is large, most people love the eastern suburb, viewing it as a paradise.

▲ Decline of the Dongdi Flower District: In the past, the flower district of Guangzhou was most lively in Dongdi. Brothels, pleasure boats, and flower boats gathered here. Now, due to the frequent impact of the current situation and military disturbances, the flower industry has suffered a great blow. The restaurants in the Dongdi area have all closed, and the brothels have also moved elsewhere. All the pleasure boats and flower boats have sailed away and moored along the Changdi area. As the saying goes, "extreme prosperity leads to decline," is it not true?

▲ Listening to Opera in the Park: To the right of the Provincial Government is the First Park. The area is quite large, and the layout is elegant and clean. Flowers and trees are planted in abundance. The park is equipped with wireless telephones. All operas broadcast by wireless radio from various places can be heard. There is also a wireless broadcasting station that broadcasts Cantonese opera several times a day. Many Cantonese people like Cantonese opera. After dusk, many people come to the park to listen quietly. The weather in Guangdong is warmer, so even in winter, the number of visitors does not decrease. Because admission to the park is free, and you can listen to songs, many citizens enjoy going there.

▲ Frequent Aircraft Training: The Aviation Department is located in Dashatou, Guangzhou. The department has an aviation school with more than a hundred students. They practice flying every day, regardless of the weather. They fly in the air with one, two, three, or four planes. I once visited Deng Yueming, the captain of the Second Air Force Squadron, and he showed me around the aviation department. The internal facilities are quite complete. The development of the aviation industry in Guangdong is boundless. Deng also recounted the experience of leading the Second Air Force Squadron on the Northern Expedition last autumn. He showed me a large sword captured from Feng Yuxiang's large sword team, saying that it was a good souvenir for their squadron.

Record of a Small Ornament Exhibition - Sun Choucheng

Zhou Shaofu from Baitazi Lane, Suzhou, is nearly sixty years old and good at carving. He has a unique and unrestrained personality. He spent thirty years and tens of thousands of yuan hand-making various small ornaments, categorizing them meticulously. He stored them in his home for his amusement. This time, at the urging of friends, he was invited to display all the small ornaments in the hall for public viewing. To prevent noise, each visitor is charged twenty cents to cover the expenses of the caretakers. (1) Three square tables are arranged in rows, displaying items used in weddings. The two lamps are only five inches tall and have the red characters "Dun Hou Tang Zhou" on them. Behind the lamps are two five-inch square red wooden tables, displaying various musical instruments such as suonas, trumpets, huqins, and strings, each only an inch long. In the main hall, everything is prepared, including chairs, teacups, and spittoons. In the bridal chamber, there is a bed about a foot long, made of mahogany, with complete bedding and curtains. Next to it are cabinets, chests, tables, and chamber pots, all smaller than an inch, but identical to the real thing. (2) A small boat is made using two high stools, representing a funeral scene. The boat is nine feet long, similar in style to the double-decked Wuxi fast boats. At the bow of the boat is a tall white archway, with the four characters "Niu Mian Bu Di" inlaid in the middle. In the front cabin is an altar with a four-inch wide and six-inch long statue of a god and a three-inch wide and four-inch high memorial tablet with a portrait of Shaofu. The tablet bears Shaofu's titles. He is still alive but does not avoid taboos, showing his open-mindedness. In the middle cabin is a coffin about eight inches long. Next to it are two wooden puppets of women, weeping by the coffin. (3) A house is built using wooden planks, about two feet high, as a model of the Zhou family ancestral hall. The entrance has wooden fences. Plaques are erected on both sides, and there are two tiger head plaques, only an inch or so in size, with the eight characters "Ancestral Hall, No Entry" written on them in red ink. Stone lions stand facing each other. A plaque hangs high above the door, creating a grand atmosphere similar to that of a Qing Dynasty yamen. (4) Three board houses are built, about five feet wide. The middle one is the longevity hall, with longevity couplets and banners hanging on all four walls. Although they are only eight or nine inches long, all the texts were specially written by famous people. The left one is the accounting room, with a mahogany accounting table about three inches high, with books, writing brushes, inkstones, abacus, and teacups on it, exquisitely crafted. The right one is the reception hall, with tables and chairs arranged like the real thing. The tea stand under the sign is equipped with everything. Everything is meticulously crafted. The Ming-style lanterns are more than an inch in diameter, with hanging tassels. (5) The kitchen is made of lead sheet, and the stove is also made of bricks, only three inches high. It also has four pots. Bamboo cabinets, water tanks, coal stoves, and other miscellaneous items are arranged on the left and right. Knives and meat blocks, everything is complete. Other items include the "Ten Thousand People Umbrella," the "Virtuous Governance Plaque," and the theatrical performances installed on the platforms. Curtains hang from the windows of the eight sedan chairs. Everything used for weddings, funerals, and celebrations, and the miscellaneous items needed for daily life are all available. To create objects so richly is rare in the world, so I am happy to record it.

Table Talk by the Wine - Qiulang

Last evening, a friend invited me to a banquet at his residence. Those at the table were all old acquaintances, and some brought their wives. The dishes were extremely rich. The host also urged us to drink diligently, so the whole table was joyful. Then someone suggested playing a drinking game, saying that social banquets often use drinking games to help the atmosphere, but this is noisy and intrusive, with little pleasure to be said. Tonight, we can tell a story or a joke to serve as a drinking game, but it must be interesting above all. Everyone agreed. Thus, everyone used their clever tongues, and laughter arose. I will choose the witty ones to record here to amuse you.

▲ Returning to Suzhou and Hangzhou: Friend A said, "There is a saying, 'Above there is heaven, below there are Suzhou and Hangzhou.' This is because Suzhou and Hangzhou have beautiful scenery, a mild climate, and abundant products, all of which are enough to arouse the envy of people from other places. Even more so, people from the northern provinces of Yan and Ji yearn for this famous paradise. In fact, those of us who grow up here do not feel any particular pleasure. It is said that when relatives or friends in the north pass away, the plain scrolls they send, with the gold characters written on them, often use the four characters 'Return to Suzhou and Hangzhou' and hang them in the courtyard. This has the same meaning as 'Return to Penglai Island' or 'Return to Yaochi' used by southerners. However, the yearning of people there for Suzhou and Hangzhou can be seen here."

▲ God-Given Rice Flour: Ten days ago, the weather was cold and freezing. Six-petaled snowflakes fluttered about, and the jade buildings and towers suddenly became a silver world. Those who wear fur coats and sit around the fireplace are three feet deep in the snow and do not know the cold. But the poor scholars and poor households who seek warmth and food day and night, because of the heavy snowfall, cannot go out to work and lament in their homes. It is truly pitiful. A friend at the table said, "It is said that in the past, when the weather was cold and the year was ending, Heaven, pitying those who were poor and had nothing to spend the year, flew down rice flour. Each household would sweep the flour in front of their doors and use it to survive the year. Later, because people were cunning and greedy, they snatched from each other and even caused deaths. Thus, what fell was snow instead of flour." Although the story is absurd and baseless, it is interesting.

Tune: Huanxi Sha - Xuange

▲ Returning Home Late from White Cloud Tower

The lamps resemble dense stars, the moon a jade scepter. My homesickness seems to be level with the white clouds. Where can I entrust my longing in this layered tower? I have poured tea and wine repeatedly, but I am already old. I have thrown gold coins secretly, but my wishes are hard to fulfill. When will I plant beans and return home with a hoe?

Two Poems on Plum Blossoms - Shuqin

Dark clouds cover the earth, jade dust flies in the sky. It is the winter vacation. I am deeply happy to have plum blossoms as companions. Therefore, I compose these poems.

A pure heart and simple nature reveal innocence. The scenery on the ridge is especially divine. The plum is willing to bring white snow to the green mountains. But the recluse Lin Bu has passed away; who else remains?

A secluded affection is difficult to reconcile with vulgarity. In a clear dream, I see her radiant, slender form on jade steps. I often linger within the sparse shadows. In the vast expanse of white stones, whom am I waiting for?

A Loyal Dog's Tragic Death During Antarctic Exploration - Zhi Zheng

Major Byrd of the United States, along with more than fifty team members, went to Antarctica for exploration in the winter of 1928 and achieved great success, adding a remarkable feat to the scientific community. The details of the team's exploration were translated and published by Zhi Zheng in Travel Magazine (Volumes 5, Issues 1 to 4). Major Byrd loved a sled dog most in his life and named him Alasca. They were inseparable. During the Antarctic expedition, Byrd assigned him to be the leader of the sled dog team, and he was unparalleled in loyalty and bravery. When Byrd returned to his country, the dog also became famous. Unfortunately, on the road in Monroe, Louisiana, he was crushed to death by a car. Those who heard of it mourned deeply. Byrd was especially saddened. He was buried a few days ago. The funeral was attended by more than two thousand officials, students, boy scouts, and civilians. It was truly an unprecedented event, and it shows how much foreigners value those who contribute to science.

Warmth in the Heart (375) Bao Tianxiao

Chapter Seventeen: The Art of Preserving Youthful Beauty Mingles with Eyebrow Makeup, Continuing the Endless Search for Thoroughbreds in the Golden Market

In reality, China doesn't need the newest types of weaponry. When two enemies fight, if the opponent uses a certain weapon, we should use the same one. This is like meeting a knife with a knife, a spear with a spear. China's enemies now are also using those old weapons. So, if we are just slightly better than them, that is enough. Even for those old weapons, we still have to ask for them from abroad. That is a very sad thing for China. Because Ye Tonghou was very well-known in Shanghai and could speak some basic English, the Pacific Trading Company hired him as a Chinese manager. Most of his friends were also revolutionaries. Any arms deals were conducted secretly through him. He socialized a lot and had wide connections. As a result, almost everyone in the northern brothels of Shanghai knew about "Third Young Master Ye." Today he came and asked Hua Yuanchun, "Old Six, I heard you're going to Beijing?" Hua Yuanchun said, "How did you know? That's really fast information! Who told you?" Ye Tonghou said, "I knew a long time ago. I always pay attention to current events. When are you leaving?" Hua Yuanchun said, "The day after tomorrow night. I've never been to Beijing before. I don't know if I'll get used to living there. I heard it's very cold." Ye Tonghou said, "Although the weather is a bit colder than Shanghai, it doesn't matter. Because the houses in the north all have stoves. I actually think the climate in Beijing is better than in the south. The kind of humidity and the rainy season in the south doesn't exist in the north. And there are many sunny days. Once, I lived in Beijing for three months. It hardly rained at all. I'm going to Beijing again soon. Maybe I'll leave next week. Hua Yuanchun was worried that she wouldn't be able to find familiar clients in Beijing. Also, Third Young Master Ye was generous to the women in the brothels, and their relationship wasn't bad. So she said, "Third Young Master, are you really coming to Beijing? Then you must come to see me! You can just ask at Qing Yu Tang. If I'm not working, I'll be staying at the Central Hotel or other hotels. I'm afraid I'll have no one to rely on in Beijing. If you come, I'll treat you like family." Ye Tonghou said, "You're saying that now. Once you get to Beijing and make a few good clients, you won't care about us old friends anymore." Hua Yuanchun said, "Third Young Master, since you say we're old friends, you should know my, Hua Old Six's, personality. Of course, people who work in brothels always want to make some money. But I'm not someone who only cares about money. If I only cared about money, I wouldn't be so poor that I have to find ways to get even a small amount of money. Old friends are always old friends. If you say that, it doesn't sound like we're old friends." Ye Tonghou laughed, "I was just joking. Why are you getting so worked up? I'll definitely come to see you in Beijing." As he spoke, he tugged at her sleeve and said, "Let me talk to you for a moment."

Local News

The Amnesty Committee of the Garrison Command Decides to Temporarily Adjourn

▲ All political prisoner cases have been reviewed.

▲ A total of forty-eight people have been released.

The Military Law Review Committee of the Songhu Garrison Command handled the amnesty of political prisoners. At the first review meeting, eighteen political prisoners, including Meng Jilu, were released. At the second meeting, twelve, including Qiu Luanxie, were released. At the third meeting, eighteen, including Wang Weibai, were released. The fourth meeting was adjourned due to lack of quorum. A total of forty-eight political prisoners have been released. Yesterday, from 1:00 PM to 3:00 PM, the fifth meeting was held again at the Longhua Command. Committee members Zhou Shida, Dai Yuanchuan, Liu Tongyi, Su Fuchou, and Zhong Huan, five people in total, decided that all political prisoner cases had been reviewed and the committee should temporarily adjourn. A report will be compiled and submitted to the Ministry of Military and Political Affairs for record. According to one committee member, this is a temporary adjournment, not a complete disbandment. If special cases are submitted requesting review, a temporary meeting will be convened at any time.

Converting the Confucius Temple into a Park

▲ Preserving the historical site of the Confucius Temple

▲ The San Sen Company wins the bid

Since the Shanghai Municipal Government decided to renovate the Confucius Temple and convert it into a park for citizens to relax, the Municipal Bureau of Public Works was ordered to plan the first phase of the renovation project and invite bids for construction on a scheduled basis. Yesterday (the 26th) at 2:00 PM, the bids were opened. The Municipal Government sent a special representative to the bureau to supervise. The plans for the Confucius Temple renovation and the results of the bidding are recorded as follows:

▲ Renovation Plan for the Confucius Temple The Confucius Temple is located on a very large site, bordered by Confucius Temple Road to the south, Xuegong Street to the east, Menghualou Street to the north, and Laodaoqing Street to the west, covering an area of approximately thirty-two acres. As the Confucius Temple is one of the historical sites in the city and the halls have been in disrepair for many years, the Bureau of Public Works has decided that those with historical value will be preserved as they are. The Dacheng Hall, Chongsheng Temple, Minglun Hall, and Kuixing Pavilion are all to be preserved. The Jukui Hall will be converted into a music hall. At the main gate and second gate of the Confucius Temple, a library will be built. The river at the Dacheng Gate will be filled in for twenty-four meters (approximately eight zhang). The original stone bridge will be removed and rebuilt about six feet to the north. The corridors on both sides of the Dashi Hall will also be removed and replaced with passages for planting trees. The school site of Minglun Primary School will be preserved as is. Because the Pan Pool floods every year during the two flood seasons, the water overflows into the classrooms of Minglun Primary School, the Pan Pool will be dredged at the time of reconstruction to prevent future flooding. The drainage ditch in Confucius Temple Road is currently under construction. The facilities in the park will be built in phases.

▲ Results of Yesterday's Bidding Yesterday was the day for the Bureau of Public Works to open the bids. Around 2:00 PM, representatives from the Municipal Government arrived at the bureau to supervise. The bidders also arrived one after another. The winning bidder was the San Sen Construction Company, with a bid of 9,946.60 yuan. Wang Yuxing and Zhu Senji, among others, were not selected because their bids were too high, one being over 16,700 yuan and the other being over 14,900 yuan.

The Municipal Government Requests the Withdrawal of Foreign Soldiers from the Outer Road

▲ Letter to the French Consul General

The Municipal Government sent a letter to the French Consul General in Shanghai, Koklin, yesterday, stating: "Dear Sir, We have received your letter stating that the case of French sailors injuring citizen Ding Jiaxun and others at Tianyao Bridge has been settled peacefully. This government has ordered the Public Security Bureau to investigate and confirm the facts. However, the matter of stationing troops in the outer road was not mentioned. The area where the sailors are stationed is within the city limits and they are undisciplined, causing repeated incidents. We have repeatedly asked your office to punish the perpetrators and provide compensation, but you have not said a word about withdrawing the sailors. This government feels deeply regretful about this. Since the sailors have repeatedly committed violence and the relationship with the local residents has deteriorated, who will be responsible if other incidents occur? We request that your Consul General consider the friendship between our countries and take measures to quickly withdraw the sailors and ensure that they will not be stationed there again in the future, in order to clarify national rights. We hope that you will investigate the aforementioned case and reply."

Dispute Between New and Old Stewards on the Gonghe Steamer

▲ Many old stewards were injured in the assault.

▲ The comprador, Shen Huating, was detained.

▲ The perpetrators will be handed over to the court today.

The Gonghe Steamer, which runs between Shanghai and Hankou under Jardine Matheson & Co., experienced a dispute because the newly appointed comprador demanded a security deposit from the old stewards without success. He also recruited new stewards to replace them, but to no avail. The new stewards assaulted the old stewards with weapons in Wuhu the day before yesterday, injuring many. The steamer arrived in port yesterday at 1:00 PM. The details of the investigation are recorded below:

▲ Existing Stewards The Gonghe Steamer of Jardine Matheson & Co. operates on the Shanghai-Hankou route and docks at the Gonghexiang Wharf in Hongkou, Shanghai. When the previous comprador, Gao Wenbin, took over, he brought thirty-eight stewards, each of whom was charged a security deposit by Gao. There were three types: 300 yuan for the first-class cabin, 180 yuan for the cabin, and 140 yuan for the third-class cabin. However, there were also eighty old stewards on the steamer, all of whom were members of the China Seamen's Union. They had never paid a security deposit under previous compradores, so Gao continued the practice and did not ask. Everyone got along well until Gao transferred his position to Shen Huating.

▲ Refusal to Pay Security Deposit The new comprador, Shen, had previously served as a comprador on the Wanliu Steamer on the Fujian route, the Dongting Steamer on the Shanghai-Hankou route, and the Jiangtian Steamer on the Hankou route under the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. Later, the Wanliu Steamer's business deteriorated and the authorities ordered it to cease operations. The Dongting Steamer also encountered danger and sank mid-route. Shen lost both positions one after another, but he continued to work on the Jiangtian Steamer. Shen then sought the position of comprador on the Gonghe Steamer. Coincidentally, the comprador of the steamer, Gao Wenbin, intended to resign, and they quickly reached an agreement. After Gao resigned, it was agreed that Shen would be responsible for the security deposits of the thirty-eight stewards Gao had previously collected. After taking over, Shen saw that there were eighty old stewards and believed that they should also pay a security deposit to be fair. However, the eighty stewards insisted that there had been no such requirement under previous compradores and firmly refused.

▲ Forcing the Surrender of Licenses Shen, unable to get his way, recruited forty new stewards and charged each of them a security deposit: 400 yuan for the first-class cabin, 300 yuan for the cabin, and 200 yuan for the third-class cabin. The new stewards prepared to board the steamer and take over, but the old stewards refused to step down, preventing the new stewards from working. They could only sit and sleep on the steamer, and their meals were provided by Shen. Seeing that this could not continue, on the evening of the 19th of this month, the steamer docked in Shanghai. Shen hired several strong men to board the steamer and force the old stewards to surrender their licenses. Yuan Dequan, the first-class cabin leader, refused and was slapped twice by Shen. Seeing that things were not going well, the old stewards also hired several people to board the steamer and protest. Shen seized the opportunity to escape. That night, all the new stewards packed up and went ashore. The next day (the 20th), the steamer set sail for Hankou as scheduled. Unexpectedly, the new stewards were waiting in Wuhu, ready to fight.

▲ A Brutal Assault Earlier, the new stewards and others left the steamer and, led by Shen, boarded another steamer to Wuhu. They also hired dozens of thugs, each wearing a badge. The new stewards each had two round black rubber plasters on their temples, and three others wore white cloth knots on their chests for identification. They prepared a large number of iron tools and waited for orders. At 4:45 AM on the day before yesterday (the 25th), the steamer arrived in Wuhu. Led by Shen, the new stewards swarmed aboard and dragged the old stewards off the steamer without asking any questions. Many stewards were sleeping and were dragged out of bed and beaten. The entire steamer was in chaos. More than twenty old stewards were dragged to the Wuhu wharf and beaten. Those who were not dragged away were brutally beaten on the steamer. Many third-class passengers were also affected.

▲ Details of the Injuries Cui Wanxi, an old steward, had his head broken by an iron ruler and bled profusely, suffering serious injuries. Yang Guisheng, Wu Zhilian, and others were also beaten by the new stewards. Yang and Wu were left in Wuhu for treatment due to their serious injuries, while Cui Wanxi was taken back to Shanghai on the steamer and sent to Renji Hospital yesterday for treatment. The whereabouts of the other stewards who were dragged to Wuhu are unknown. It is not known where they are, or if they were injured. Ding Rongchang, another old steward, was hung up and handcuffed in the cabin for two days and nights. He was finally rescued yesterday when the steamer arrived in Shanghai.

▲ Crew Members Evacuate During the fight, the crew members, fearing that they would be affected, fled to their cabins and locked the doors, not daring to come out. The shipowner, Kang Bier, originally planned to sound the alarm and ask the British soldiers from nearby warships to come and stop the fighting, but the comprador, Shen, dissuaded him, saying that it was just a matter of expelling the old stewards and there was no need for foreign soldiers to interfere. After the fighting, the old stewards who had not been dragged away did not dare to go to the main cabin, fearing that they would be beaten again. They took refuge in the cargo hold and engine room. Their duties were performed by the new stewards who boarded the steamer in Wuhu.

▲ Telegram for Help When the Gonghe Steamer arrived in Nanjing on the 25th, the injured old stewards secretly went ashore and sent a telegram to Shanghai, reporting to the union that more than twenty colleagues had been beaten and taken away in Wuhu and their whereabouts were unknown. They asked the union to provide assistance. Upon receiving the telegram, the union reported to the Shanghai Water and Land Police Bureau, asking them to arrest the perpetrators when the steamer arrived.

▲ Comprador Detained The steamer stayed in Wuhu for two hours and then sailed to Nanjing. Shen disembarked at Xiaguan and took a train back to Shanghai. However, the Shanghai Seamen's Union had already received the report and sent people to wait at the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway Station. Shen was spotted by union members on the night train and reported to the railway police, who arrested him. It was reported that Shen was carrying a handgun, which was also seized by the police. Both the person and the gun were temporarily held at the railway station, pending transfer to the local court for disposition.

▲ Perpetrators Arrested At 1:20 PM yesterday, the steamer arrived in port. The Water Police Bureau had received a letter from the Seamen's Union in the morning, requesting the arrest of the culprits. The captain ordered West Detective Pang Shi, Chinese Detectives Cheng Yongnian, Huang Zhenlin, Deng Jiageng, Hu Changqing, Wu Rongsheng, and Huang Songsheng to lead more than twenty Chinese and foreign armed police officers to board small boats and guard the steamer to prevent the culprits from escaping. At the same time, the Public Concession Police also sent several armed detectives to assist. After the steamer docked, the Water Police Bureau officers boarded the steamer and conducted a thorough search. They found three iron bars, three axes, two knives, two iron chains, and more than twenty iron rods in the new stewards' quarters. They then encountered Hu Hanzhang, the leader of the new stewards, and interrogated him. His face turned pale. He claimed to be the steamer's purser and was going to see the passengers, but the old stewards recognized him and reported him to the detectives. He was immediately detained, along with Ding Yongchang, the leader of the old stewards, and taken back to the police station. The weapons used in the assault were also taken to the police station for safekeeping.

▲ Transfer to Court The captain first conducted a preliminary hearing for the two. According to Ding, he was the leader of the old stewards and described the entire incident in detail. He claimed that when the fight broke out, he hid in the mailman's coat closet, but Shen spotted him and dragged him out. Shen ordered his men to cut off his foot with an axe, but they were persuaded to stop. He was then imprisoned in a room. According to Hu Hanzhang, he was from Anhui and had gone to Anqing on business. He returned to Wuhu and asked when the Shanghai steamer would arrive. He was told that the Gonghe Steamer would pass by on the morning of the 25th, so he boarded the steamer to return to Shanghai. He denied being the leader of the new stewards and claimed to know nothing about the new stewards' assault. The captain ordered them to be detained, pending transfer of the defendants and weapons to the local court today for questioning.

Shanghai County Holds Budget Meeting Yesterday

▲ Passing the Levy of Agricultural Fees for Autonomous Funding

The Shanghai County Government has recently received an order from the Provincial Government to submit the budget for the 20th year. County Magistrate Yan convened a budget meeting yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, gathering more than ten people from various county agencies, including the heads of various bureaus, district chiefs, the head of the property management office, and the county agricultural station. County Magistrate Yan, as the chairman, began by reporting that the county's local funding was insufficient. The county agricultural station had no funding and had to borrow from the county's internal affairs funds in the 19th year's budget, which made it difficult to carry out county affairs. Therefore, it was proposed to request approval from the Provincial Government to levy an additional five percent on the busy season tax to be used as agricultural improvement funds. The funding for each district was also insufficient, and the autonomous affairs were heavy. It was proposed to levy an additional amount from the deed and tooth tax, similar to the construction donation, starting from the 20th year to be used for district purposes. The Finance Bureau then presented the prepared draft budget, which was discussed item by item by the attendees. It was resolved to pass the proposal as is. The meeting then adjourned.

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Requests the Cancellation of the Railway Traffic Surtax

▲ Telegram to the Ministry of Railways

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram to the Ministry of Railways in Nanjing yesterday, stating: "To the esteemed Ministry of Railways in Nanjing, The collection of the traffic surtax on the Jinghu and Huhang railways originated during the time of Sun Chuanfang in Jiangsu. After the National Government settled the Southeast, this surtax was explicitly abolished by the Ministry. Not long after, it was reinstated in the name of reorganizing traffic. Over the years, we have observed that public opinion is that passenger and freight fares on the Jinghang railways have already increased compared to the past. If, in addition to the official increase, a surtax is created, it seems to contradict the purpose of facilitating public transportation. This is the first point. The tracks and vehicles of the Jinghang railways have been damaged by military operations, which is different from the situation on the Longhai and Jinpu railways. The so-called reorganization of traffic seems to be unfounded. Moreover, these two railways are located in the important areas of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, and their business is booming, with annual surpluses. Even if the Ministry has plans for reorganization and expansion, it is the duty of the state-owned railways to take from the business surplus and not add to the burden of passengers. This is the second point. In addition to the passenger tickets being collected at a progressive rate of two percent, freight transport is charged at seven percent. Traditionally, shipping is cheaper than rail transport. Since the abolition of the customs posts, the obstacles to water transport have also been removed. However, the railway traffic surtax still exists, which is equivalent to leaving a mutated kind of internal revenue tax. This increasingly causes commercial freight to shift to water transport. This is detrimental to the government's new policy of abolishing internal revenue taxes and hinders the railways from undertaking freight transport services. This is the third point. Based on the reasons listed above, it is absolutely necessary to abolish this traffic surtax immediately. We hereby submit this information to the Ministry for your review and approval. Please consider public opinion and order the two railway bureaus to stop collecting the traffic surtax from today onwards for the sake of public convenience. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce respectfully bows."

The People's Livelihood Research Association Holds Its Fourth Meeting Yesterday

▲ Discussing Workers' Welfare Issues Today

The People's Livelihood Improvement Research Association continued its fourth meeting yesterday to discuss modern industrial problems. More than sixty representatives from various regions attended, divided into two sessions in the morning and afternoon. Li Peien was the chairman and Zhang Shizhang was the recorder. The details of the meeting are recorded as follows:

▲ Agenda Items In the morning: (A) Wang Yunwu proposed that, based on the world trend and China's needs, it is necessary to adopt large-scale industries. However, the preconditions are (1) organizational issues, (2) labor-capital issues, and (3) solutions. For the first issue, scientific management methods must be used. However, the Chinese people have misunderstandings about scientific management and are afraid that after implementation, there will be overproduction and unemployment problems. In fact, the cause of unemployment in Europe and America is not the result of using scientific management. For example, the unemployment problem in Germany is due to the loss of territory and the reduction of the military, not the fault of scientific management. Scientific management can make workers' compensation sufficient and treatment fair. For the second issue, a profit-sharing system can be used to allow the labor side to share the surplus of the industry, so that labor and capital can cooperate. For the third method, factory meetings should be adopted, and labor and capital should jointly seek work and business improvements. Only after the implementation of the above three methods can China's large-scale industry have hope. After Wang finished speaking, Chen Qitian raised various difficulties in the implementation of these three methods in the West, which seemed unable to completely solve the labor-capital problem. In the afternoon, Deng Yuzhi proposed: (1) Why do female workers account for the majority in large factories? (2) How should the daily working hours of up to twelve hours be improved? (3) How should the poor living conditions of workers be improved? (4) How should the lack of education and entertainment for workers be improved? (5) The wage difference between child labor and adult labor is too large, so many factories use child labor. (6) Female workers are unable to take care of their children due to work. (7) The solution to various problems still lies in government power, national laws, and labor unions and other methods.

Negotiations Regarding the Autopsy of Zhang Wenyi’s Corpse

Zhang Wenyi, the garrison battalion commander of the Wusong Fortress Command, was sent to Baolong Hospital for treatment due to a ruptured blood vessel in his nose. He passed away in the hospital at 10:35 AM on the 20th of this month. His younger brother, Zhang Wenyu, special affairs chief Wang Wumu of the garrison battalion, and clerk Ji Xuzhong were present to care for him. The body was moved to the morgue. The next day, his family members went to the hospital for inspection and were shocked to discover a knife wound running from the neck to the lower right leg, which had been stitched up.

Photographing Zhang Wenyi’s Corpse After Dissection

It was clear that the hospital had secretly dissected the body. Zhang Wenyu reported the situation to Commander Deng of the Fortress Command, who sent Deputy Adjutant Shen to the hospital for negotiation. The hospital director, Dr. Bader (transliteration), received him and provided a written explanation of the dissection. After Deputy Adjutant Shen returned to report, Commander Deng reported the facts to the Ministry of Military Administration and sent a letter to Baolong Hospital to question them. Yesterday, the ministry sent personnel to the hospital to transport Zhang's body back to the Wusong Fortress, where it will be coffined and buried after Zhang's father arrives in Song. Negotiations with the hospital are underway.

Resolution of Labor Strikes at Two Factories

▲Arbitration Ruling at Tianzhang Factory

A labor strike occurred at the Pudong factory of Tianzhang Paper Company due to workers demanding year-end bonuses and the reinstatement of workers Zhao Yaojin and Chen Qichang. The Social Affairs Bureau convened a mediation committee three times, but no resolution was reached due to the company's insistence. According to the Labor Dispute Resolution Law, the mediation was declared unsuccessful, and the city government was asked to apply for arbitration. All workers, because the company did not comply with the government's advice, had no choice but to go on strike from the 9th to awaken the company and request assistance from all sectors. The municipal government, to avoid expanding the labor strike, convened an arbitration committee on the 20th for arbitration. The chairman was Guo [name missing], and the committee members were Hou Dachun, Yu Zhong, Zuo De [name missing],

Zhao Zhenyao, and Chen Liangyu, with Chen Tianzhou as the recorder. The workers were immediately ordered to resume work and await arbitration. All workers complied and resumed work. The arbitration committee ruled that (1) the factory should pay a year-end bonus equivalent to ten days' wages to each worker; (2) no wages will be paid for the strike period; (3) workers Zhao Yaojin and Chen Qichang should be reinstated, and their wages should be reduced by half during the suspension period.

▲Mediation Success at Ruirong Factory

The British-owned Ruirong Iron Factory on Yangshupu Road employs over 300 male workers. The labor-management relationship has been harmonious. In March of last year, the Social Affairs Bureau and both parties signed labor-management conditions regarding treatment issues. Later, due to poor business, the factory adjusted the shifts of the original workers. The labor side had no objection, because this was stipulated in the conditions. Recently, business has improved, but the factory has not restored the original system. On the 24th, the labor side sent representatives to demand a restoration, but the new foreman, Mr. Smith, refused, leading to a work slowdown by all workers on the 25th. The factory then requested the Social Affairs Bureau to send personnel to mediate. The bureau sent section member Gu Bingyuan to persuade them, and both parties agreed on three resolutions: (1) The factory acknowledges that everything will be handled in accordance with the labor-management conditions, but before the conditions expire on March 12th, no further shift adjustments may be made; (2) Starting today, the factory should restore the non-shift adjustment

Page 10

system; (3) All workers will resume work today, and wages will not be deducted for the work slowdown period. All workers resumed work that afternoon.

Jiang-Zhejiang Postal Service Requests Modified Registration Regulations

▲Private Postal Services Still Allowed to Deliver Inland Letters

Yin Yuantong and other representatives of the Jiang-Zhejiang Postal Service Association submitted a document to the National Government, stating that the revised registration regulations are still difficult to comply with, and requesting modifications based on previous regulations to maintain the people's livelihood. The document stated that it is difficult to comply with the regulations regarding private postal services delivering inland letters, and requested modified registration regulations to maintain the people's livelihood. The Ministry of Communications approved the request, stating, "Having received your submission, we have instructed the Postal Administration to revise Article 5 of the regulations for private postal services obtaining registration certificates. You should apply for registration certificates in accordance with the regulations." This approval was based on the Postal Administration's revised Article 5, which stated that all letters collected by private postal services must be sealed in total packages and delivered to the post office for delivery. However, if the place of origin or destination does not have a post office or mailbox, or cannot be reached by village postmen, the private postal service may temporarily deliver the letters themselves. However, if there are two or more post offices along the way, and the private postal service also has branches or agents there, the letters should still be delivered through the post office. The private postal service should provide a list of the locations of its offices and agents to the local post office for record-keeping. Thus, inland letters must still be delivered through the post office. The so-called revision is no different from no revision. Private postal services are mostly established in urban areas or famous towns, and all urban areas or famous towns have post offices or mailboxes. Therefore, all inland letters must be delivered through the post office, and private postal services will have no livelihood. As for the statement that private postal services may temporarily deliver letters themselves if the place of origin or destination does not have a post office or mailbox, or cannot be reached by village postmen, it is argued that the destination may be a remote village without a post office or beyond the reach of postmen, but the place of origin must be a major trading port or a town with a post office or mailbox. It is almost impossible for both the place of origin and destination to have no post office. Therefore, the so-called permission to deliver letters themselves is only in name and not in practice, and will inevitably force all private postal services to close down. It is recalled that when the postal service was first established, inland letters collected by the post office were delivered by private postal services without any charge. Overseas letters collected by private postal services were sealed in total packages and delivered to the post office, with postage paid. The post office and private postal services were closely linked, and foreign and inland transportation was convenient. Private postal services were actually auxiliary to the post office. For decades, private postal services have been allowed to deliver inland letters themselves for this reason. The situation in China is different from that in other countries. In other countries, cities and villages have telegraphs, telephones, trains, and cars, and transportation is convenient. Postal delivery is unimpeded, and commerce and public sentiment are not hindered. Private postal services have no foothold. China has a vast territory, and villages are numerous. Telegraphs and telephones have not been widely installed, and trains and cars have not reached the entire country. The delivery of inland letters relies entirely on human labor. Once private postal services cease operations, it will inevitably obstruct inland commerce and information, paralyze the market, and prevent letters from reaching remote villages. Commerce and public sentiment will be hampered, and the livelihoods of over 100,000 poor people in the postal service industry will be pitiful. After careful consideration, the representatives unanimously agreed to request the government to take into account the situation and allow private postal services to continue to deliver inland letters themselves according to previous regulations. In the future, as transportation develops and postal delivery is unimpeded, merchants and the public will voluntarily use the post office, and private postal services will be naturally eliminated. This will benefit both commerce and the people's livelihood. Therefore, we dare to submit this request to your government for review and approval."

Rent Dispute at Shoufu Lane, Caishi Road, French Concession

▲Tenants Petition Various Agencies for Assistance

The tenants of Shoufu Lane, Caishi Road, French Concession, submitted documents to the Municipal Government, the Municipal Party Committee, and the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, stating, "We are petitioning because the landlord is arbitrarily increasing rent and demanding the signing of illegal lease contracts that are extremely harsh and unacceptable. We request that you take measures to stop this to benefit the people's livelihood. The tenants have been living and doing business in the houses in Shoufu Lane, Caishi Road, French Concession, for over eight years. The landlord was initially Nongcheng Company. In November of the 12th year of the Republic of China, the property was sold to a Wu surname, a compradore of Hua Bi Bank. The lease matters were entrusted to Yipin Bank. At that time, the rent was increased once. It was also increased once in January of last year. Therefore, the current rent is not only low compared to the rent in the neighborhood, but it is also several yuan higher. However, on January 10th of this year, we suddenly received a notice from Yong'an Real Estate Company, stating that the lease matters had been transferred to the company for management and that all tenants must sign a lease contract, otherwise they would be deemed to have waived their rights and would be required to vacate the premises. The tenants contacted the company, but the company re-established the rent, calculated monthly in silver, and increased the original rent by a significant amount. A lease contract must also be signed. Upon reviewing the contents of the contract, it is extremely harsh (the lease contract is attached for review). If we agree, the tenants will have almost no place to live. Moreover, at a time when commerce is declining and the people's livelihood is difficult, repeated rent increases are unbearable. We have repeatedly sent letters through representatives, but the company has ignored them. On February 20th, they sent letters to all tenants, demanding that they sign the contract within one week and implement the rent increase. All tenants are very panicked. We believe that such a harsh contract is rare in the city. Moreover, the tenants have been paying rent monthly without incident. When Yipin Bank managed the lease previously, there were no

[illegible words] This time, the company took over the management and immediately took this initiative, increasing the rent significantly, treating the tenants as fish to be slaughtered, hoping to extract a large income. If this is not stopped, I am afraid that landlords throughout the city will follow suit, having a great impact on the livelihood of ordinary people. We have always admired your care for the people's livelihood and your empathy. For this illegal and harsh lease contract and the overreach of forcibly increasing rent, we beg you to provide assistance and stop it to benefit the people's livelihood and reduce the burden. This will be a great benefit," February 26th.

Cotton Weaving Industry Decides to Increase Dyeing Prices

The Shanghai Silk Light Cotton Weaving Industry Association convened a meeting of dye factory operators yesterday afternoon, attended by over 20 representatives. The chairman, Zhu Wenqi, reported the purpose of the meeting, stating that the prices of all raw materials in the industry, such as caustic soda, sulfuric acid, and dyes, have been rising continuously. Therefore, it was legally decided that from March 1st, regardless of new or old set lines, all dyeing, starting from the original light, will be increased by 1.5 liang to maintain the cost, and the dyeing prices will be announced to all customers.

Cheng Yongxi Accused of Communist Suspicion

▲Previous Punishment Revoked Due to Lack of Evidence

▲Yesterday, the Special Court's Criminal Court Held a Trial

In December of last year, the Municipal Public Security Bureau discovered that Cheng Yongxi, a Western doctor from Anhui residing in Yimin Lane, Baike Road, was suspected of being a communist. Detectives were dispatched along with the police to detain Cheng and send him to the Special Zone Local Court. After a preliminary hearing, Cheng was ordered to be taken to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for further interrogation. After hearing the verdict, Wang Yaotang, the police lawyer, stated that according to the agreement to recover the Mixed Court, any case to be transferred must be transferred after the court investigates and clarifies the evidence. The Municipal Public Security Bureau has not presented evidence to prove it, so he expressed his disagreement and filed an objection. The collegial panel, with Judge Xu, ruled on the 9th of this month that the original punishment was revoked, and the case should be investigated and punished again. Cheng was then returned to the police custody and has been there for three weeks. Yesterday morning, the police escorted Cheng to the Second Criminal Court of the Special Court, and the Municipal Public Security Bureau still sent personnel to present a document requesting the transfer. The police lawyer, Wang Yaotang, explained the previous situation. Judge Wu Tingqi declared to the defendant that the Public Security Bureau stated that he was suspected of being a communist in Guangzhou in the 16th year of the Republic of China. He asked Cheng whether he had any explanation. Cheng replied that in the first half of the 16th year, he practiced medicine in Shanghai. Because business was bad, he followed Zhang Fakui's army as a military doctor in the second half of the year. He moved the army back to Guangzhou from Wuchang. (Q) Who was the chief military doctor? (A) Shi Yi. (Q) How many military doctors were there? (A) More than ten. (Q) Was Luo Haifeng also a military doctor? (A) I don't remember. (Q) Were you in Guangzhou at the end of the 16th year when the communists were causing trouble? (A) Yes. (Q) What was the situation at that time? (A) I only saw chaos. I also closed the door and dared not look out, and I often heard gunshots. (Q) Which army was firing? (A) Initially, Zhang Fakui's army returned to Guangzhou and then went to Dongxiang. Later, I heard that Guangzhou was surrounded and opened fire with the communist army. I also avoided it at that time. (Q) At that time, were you working with Luo Haifeng in the Red Army Hospital? (A) No. (Q) Was the Red Army a part of Zhang Fakui's army? (A) Yes, but I later entered the Medical Section of the Health Bureau, and the director was Shi Yi. Judge Wu stated that it was necessary to investigate the case further and ordered the defendant to be returned to custody for a continued trial at a later date. The defendant's lawyer requested bail, which was

rejected.

Municipal Hygiene Testing Laboratory Offers Free Rabies Vaccine Injections

▲And Free Smallpox Vaccinations

The Municipal Hygiene Testing Laboratory, recognizing the frequent occurrences of citizens being bitten by rabid dogs and using ineffective remedies, leading to deaths from rabies, is offering free rabies vaccine injections to all citizens bitten by rabid dogs. Those bitten should immediately go to the laboratory to receive the injections, free of charge. However, they must adhere to the laboratory's instructions and not interrupt the injections for them to be effective. Previously, these injections were very expensive. The laboratory's initiative to provide free injections is truly beneficial to the citizens. Fresh vaccine is also being used for smallpox vaccinations. Both are available daily from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM.

Municipal Health Bureau Clinic Opening Announcement

The Municipal Health Bureau's Municipal First Clinic, located at the former site of the Zhabei Public Works and Patrol Donation Bureau on Minli Road in Zhabei, has been renovated and will open on March 3rd. The following is a summary of its regulations: (1) Registration and consultations will be held every Tuesday, Thursday, and Saturday from 9:00 AM to 11:30 AM. (2) Registration and medical fees are waived. However, if medicine is dispensed in bottles, a deposit will be charged: 10 copper coins for a large bottle, 5 copper coins for a small bottle, and 2 copper coins for an earthenware jar. The deposit will be refunded upon return of the bottle or jar. (3) Patients must see the doctor in order and should not jump the queue. (4) The clinic treats internal medicine, surgery, dermatology, venereology, ophthalmology, and otolaryngology. All medications for venereal diseases must be provided by the patient. Medications for all other departments will be provided by the clinic. (5) The clinic's doctors will not make house calls for the time being. (6) Consultation hours are subject to change.

▲Tobacco Dealers Resolved Yesterday

The Bureau of Unified Taxation has ordered all distributors of matches in the city to register their stock with the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Unified Taxation Bureau on Weihaiwei Road by the 28th of this month and obtain a certificate for immediate transport and sale. This news caused panic among tobacco dealers, as they have the widest distribution network for both wholesale and retail sales and therefore the largest inventory. However, their sales have been established for a long time and cannot be pre-determined, making the situation significantly different. The trade association specially sent representatives to petition but were unsuccessful. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, the members gathered at the Shanghai South Office to re-discuss the outbound transport policy. Director Qian expressed his opinion that although the association had already issued notices regarding match stock, he feared that members had not fully paid attention and were not aware. As the petition had been ineffective and re-issuing notices was impossible due to the imminent deadline, he urged all attendees to fulfill their obligations and verbally notify their counterparts to prepare for outbound transport and sale to avoid misunderstandings and tax penalties during inspections. This was unanimously approved. Next, Gaochang Temple Xieji Sheng reported on a request to reduce the tax on light tobacco and alcohol licenses. It was resolved to appoint Qian Wenda and Qiu Tanglin to contact the tax office and handle the matter. Finally, the meeting discussed the regulation of trade practices and labor-management cooperation for mutual development and livelihood, adjourning after 7:00 PM.

Twelve Trade Associations Use Ning-Shao Wharf as a Transit Route

▲Each Acknowledges an Annual Rent of 3,000 Yuan

Twelve trade associations in the Nanshi district of this city, including those dealing in fruits, local products, preserved meats, southern goods, oilseed, and medicinal materials, have been negotiating with Mr. Yu Qiaqing of the Sanbei Company for several days to find a solution for loading and unloading goods due to the inability to do so at the Ning-Shao Wharf. They have now reached an agreement to allow the use of the wharf as a transit route. Each of the twelve trade associations will pay an annual rent of 3,000 yuan for the wharf. Therefore, the trade associations discussed the method of apportioning the rent yesterday and notified their members that they can now use the Ning-Shao Wharf as a transit route for loading and unloading goods, benefiting commercial transport.

Following the death of Yang Deshan, the police chief of the Shanghai District Court, all court police officers jointly requested that Chief Prosecutor Liu Maochu promote police inspector Chen Xihui to fill the vacancy. However, Mr. Liu believed that although the position of police inspector was one rank below police chief, the inspector's workload was even heavier and should not be neglected due to the promotion. Therefore, he ordered Chen Xihui to remain in his original position. As for the police chief position, Mr. Liu found that Xu Jinqing, currently a detective at the Garrison Headquarters, was previously a court police inspector and was naturally familiar with the work. Therefore, he ordered Xu Jinqing to be appointed as police chief. Xu Jinqing has resigned from his position as a detective at the Garrison Headquarters and reported for duty yesterday.

The Knitwear Industry Agrees to Raise Prices

The Knitwear Trade Association recently convened a joint meeting of electrical knitting factories in the city at Yijia Chun to discuss the pricing of motorized socks. Over thirty companies attended, including Fuhua, Renyu, Jinbu, Hongxing, Gongzu, Rongyang, Sanlian, Guanghua, Zhicheng, Nanchang, Gongli, Haitong, Jinghua, Yuexing, Jiekang, Jiuyi, Sancai, Yihe, Yunhua, Gongxin, Xincheng, Dahua, Yida, and Zhengda. Cai Saqiao was elected as the temporary chairman. After everyone expressed their opinions, it was generally agreed that yarn prices have increased sharply and various raw materials have skyrocketed recently. The sales prices of various factories are difficult to fix, so temporary standard prices must be set to meet market needs. After public discussion, the following temporary prices were set: 42-count long men's socks with ribbed cuffs: 2 liang and 6 qian to 2 liang and 5 qian; 40-count long men's socks with plain cuffs: 2 liang and 8 qian and 5 fen; 60-count long men's socks with plain cuffs and soles: 3 liang and 6 qian to 3 liang and 5 qian; those with cushioned soles will add 1 qian; 60-count single-strand long men's socks with plain cuffs and cushioned soles: 3 liang and 3 qian and 5 fen to 3 liang and 5 qian.

The Humanities Monthly, Volume 2, Issue 1, Edition 1

As a monthly magazine, capable of indexing over 170 kinds of journals and listing over 1,740 kinds, it can be said that "Humanities" Monthly is the first in today's publishing industry. This year, Volume 2 has begun, seeking even more excellence, and the selection of materials is extremely cautious. Volume 2, Issue 1 has recently been published. The translations include "A Small Record of the Transmission of Song Confucian Books to Japan" translated by Gu Lu and "The Soviet Union's Five-Year Plan in the Eyes of the British and Americans" by Jian Bing, one describing the eastward transmission of Chinese culture six hundred years ago, and the other examining the attitude of the homeland towards the Soviet Union. Both are extremely important in terms of culture and economy. The notes include two articles by Jiangdong Adou and the Old Man Cherishing Yin, which are even more mellow and flavorful, making people intoxicated and reluctant to let go. This is truly one of the most valuable and interesting publications in today's publishing industry. Local News 2

Ancient Coffin and Ancient Coins Unearthed on Zhuhuo Three Roads

▲Workers Unearth While Burying Electrical Cables

▲Believed to be from the Shouyuan Period

The Da Mei Evening News reports that yesterday, workers from the Shanghai Telephone Company unearthed six coffins, three ancient coins, and four earthenware jars while burying electrical cables at the intersection of Zhubao San Road on the Bund. The workers opened two of the coffins, finding only some withered bones. However, the coffins were still intact and sturdy, taking a long time to open with axes. The remaining four coffins were spared from being opened due to the arrival of the patrol. According to eyewitnesses, the coffins were likely from the Song and Yuan dynasties, buried over 600 years ago. Unfortunately, the ancient coins had already been taken away by the workers, making it impossible to verify. It is believed that the area was once the site of tombs of gentry and wealthy families. Over the years, the descendants declined, and the area was eventually turned into a road.

A Case of Suspected Enticement and Rape with Incoherent Foster Daughter

▲Claims to have been raped and abandoned in the wilderness

▲Severely scolds Xiao Sizi for lacking conscience

▲Xie Xiao Sizi is suspected and sent to court

▲Still no results after confronting each other

Zhou Jin Di, a 16-year-old foster daughter of Zhang Hong Cai from Jiangbei, works at the Yufeng Cotton Mill in Yangshupu and lives in the mill's No. 7 workshop. She suddenly disappeared at 7:00 PM last month. On the morning of the 2nd of this month, she was found wandering on the side of the road at the intersection of Datong Road and Gonghe Road in Zhabei. Those who saw and questioned her were met with silence, appearing mentally ill. A patrol officer spotted her and took her to the Fourth District Public Security Bureau. When questioned by the officer, she remained silent. She was temporarily detained pending family recognition. Zhang Hong Cai learned of the incident and went to the bureau to identify her, confirming that she was his missing foster daughter. However, he did not know why she had lost consciousness. He sent her to the nearby Baoshan Road Hospital, where the doctor gave her medicine and injected her head. Her mind cleared slightly, and she mumbled to herself, but she still could not return to her original state. When asked about what had happened, she could not answer many questions. Later, she suddenly said sternly that Xiao Sizi had raped her and abandoned her in the wilderness, and that he lacked conscience. She then claimed that she had been raped by a young man for several nights, with an old man sitting by and witnessing it. Her remaining words were mostly incoherent. Zhang noticed that the gold earrings on her ears and the velvet shirt she was wearing were missing. Hearing her words, he suspected that she had been raped, so he asked the doctor to examine her private parts, which were indeed not intact. With no clues, it was difficult to ask the officials to investigate. He took Jin Di back, but she remained as dull as a wooden chicken, staying in the workshop without speaking or smiling. The wife of Xie Changhai, a fellow villager of hers, also works at Yufeng and lives next door to Jin Di. One afternoon, Xie visited the workshop to see his wife. Zhang suddenly remembered that Xie was also named Xiao Sizi. Before Jin Di disappeared, Xie would always visit his wife on Sundays. After this incident, he had not come for a long time. Xie was strongly suspected. Zhang reported him when he finally saw Xie yesterday, and he was sent to the Special District Local Court by the relevant police station this morning. Judge Xiao conducted a preliminary hearing. Zhang stated the previous circumstances, but Xie denied everything. When Jin Di was questioned, she only provided her name, age, and origin, and said nothing else. The court ordered Xie to stand in front of Jin Di and asked if he was the rapist, but Jin Di only glanced at him slightly, turned her head away, and gave no indication of whether it was him or not, yielding no results. Xie was detained for the time being, pending a forensic examination to determine what illness she had and whether she was a virgin, before further questioning and verification.

New Sassoon Sues Tenants Case Debate Period

▲Three Groups of Tenants Interrogated

▲Debate to Open on the 23rd of Next Month

▲Saulmon is a Real Estate Manager

▲Has Been Certified by the British Consulate

The case of 164 tenants in Qingyun Lane, North Sichuan Road, being sued by British merchant New Sassoon Company for rent arrears, requesting a judgment for compensation and ordering all tenants to move out, has been heard by Judge Zhou Daren of the Special District Local Court. The defendants were divided into four groups to be interrogated to avoid crowding. On the 23rd, the first group of 41 households was interrogated. After clarifying the fact of rent arrears, a court date was set for the 23rd of next month for debate, as reported in the newspapers. On the morning of the 24th, the second group was interrogated. The plaintiff's lawyer, Huppert, submitted a letter from Davis, the manager of the company, in response to the defense lawyer Xue Jiaqi's objection to the qualification of British citizen Saulmon, who represented New Sassoon Company in the lawsuit, on the day of the preliminary hearing. The letter proved that Saulmon was indeed the manager of the New Sassoon Real Estate Department and had the right to represent the company in the lawsuit. However, lawyer Xue still attacked the letter, saying that there was no way to verify whether the letter was signed by Davis, and its authenticity was questionable. According to the Civil Procedure Law, private certificates should be proven by the person presenting the evidence. Judge Zhou then instructed the plaintiff's lawyer to order Davis to appear in court next time to prove Saulmon's position. He then clarified the facts of rent arrears of each household and also instructed that the cases be debated together on the 23rd of next month. On the morning of the 25th, the third group was heard, but Davis still did not appear in court that day. According to the plaintiff's lawyer, he was suffering from illness. Judge Zhou asked each defendant who appeared in court about the amount they owed. The debate date was also set for March 23rd. Yesterday, Wu summoned the last group. The plaintiff's lawyer first explained that Davis's illness, according to the doctor, required him to rest quietly and that it was difficult for him to appear in court. The letter proving Saulmon's qualification has now been certified by the British Consul, which should be credible. He then submitted the letter. Judge Zhou then questioned the defendants who appeared in court and instructed that a unified decision be made after the conclusion of the debate on the morning of March 23rd. Lawyer Xue then requested that a larger courtroom be selected when the time came, as all tenants wanted to be in court.

Suicide Out of Frustration from Lack of Schooling

▲Pitiful Wang Ruqin Died for Her Ambition

Wang Jingquan, the director of the North Henan-Shandong Gunpowder Mine Refining Factory of the Ministry of Military Affairs, resides on Tauffeurs Road in the French Concession. His eldest daughter, Ruqin, is 22 years old and attends the second grade of the high school department of Jinan University in Zhenru. Recently, due to her eagerness to learn, she was eager to advance in grade. Without graduating from high school, she planned to apply for a university undergraduate course. In the middle of this month, she managed to obtain a high school diploma and went to Daxia University on Zhongshan Road to register for the examination. However, the diploma became a problem, and she was not accepted. Ruqin was ashamed and frustrated, and her depression was evident. Her father learned of this situation and, in addition to earnestly persuading her, asked a friend to help her enroll in a law and politics college to fulfill his daughter's original intention of pursuing education. However, this matter was not settled until the day before yesterday, and Ruqin, unable to wait, suddenly had a pessimistic thought and hanged herself in her bedroom that evening. This morning, her father was about to inform his daughter of the good news. However, after knocking on the door for a long time, there was no sound. He tried to pry open the door and saw his daughter hanging high, already dead. At that time, he reported the matter to the French police for collection, but the police said that the matter involved human life and had to be examined. Therefore, the body remained there for a day, and had not yet been put in a coffin last night.

Later, according to a tip from a friend, Lanzhen had become involved with Zhang Meiting, a garment worker from Pudong, and was cohabiting at No. 48 Jianyu Lane, Haichao Temple South Street, outside Xiaonanmen. According to Lanzhen, she had married Zhang Meiting as his wife two years ago through a matchmaker named Wang A'gen, based on her own decision. Incoming Correspondence Regarding Several Points of View on the Implementation of the Factory Act by Chen Zongcheng

The National Government has promulgated the Factory Act, which is now officially ordered to be implemented on August 1st of this year. From the perspective of the International Labour Office, this is truly something to congratulate the National Government on, and to celebrate and comfort our country's society. As for the implementation of the Factory Act, there should be no further delays, and the government naturally has appropriate arrangements for the subsequent steps and preparations for the implementation of the Factory Act. In my opinion, the following are the points that we urgently need to pay attention to at present: (1) Training and protection of factory inspectors, (2) Standardization of the implementation of the Factory Act in various factories in the country, (3) Labor and management organizations should do their best to assist the government in the implementation of the Factory Act. The above three points are briefly explained as follows: (1) A complete inspection system is indeed the most important condition for the successful implementation of the Factory Act. The National Government, in view of this, has already promulgated the Factory Inspection Law, but there are still several practical problems that are worthy of our attention. A. The training of inspectors seems to require many experienced people to actively guide practical training, and special training should be added for specialized issues such as preventing machine hazards and improving factory hygiene. Suitable inspectors are actually the most difficult to obtain. B. The selection and appointment of inspectors must be strict, but the number does not necessarily need to be large, because the number of factories in our country with more than 3,000 people is still small. Looking at Japan's 1925 factory inspection report, Japan had 300 inspectors, and 27,000 factories were subject to the Factory Act. 47,000 factory inspections were conducted that year. Japan's factory inspection experience can be very useful for our reference. C. The position of the inspector must have considerable protection, so that they can perform their duties without fear of slander. Inspectors must receive a relatively high salary, so that they are economically independent and not tempted by profit. The duties and environment of inspectors are very special, so the above points should be noted. (2) The Factory Act should be uniform for both Chinese and foreign factories in the future. The importance of this point need not be elaborated. At the first session of the International Labour Conference, it was approved that all countries enjoying concessions and other extraterritorial rights in China should adopt the same measures in the concessions or concession lands in accordance with the labor laws already established by the Chinese government, or implement the labor laws formulated by the Chinese government. International public opinion is paying so much attention to this, and countries such as England, France, and Japan have long implemented advanced factory laws to protect their own workers. In my opinion, if this issue is given appropriate attention, it should not be difficult to resolve it satisfactorily. (3) The effectiveness of the Factory Act after its implementation also lies in the help of labor and management. Article 16 of the Factory Inspection Law promulgated by the government states that "Factory inspectors shall provide opinions to the factory and workers on increasing safety and preventing dangers, and shall devise ways to make both parties cooperate to improve the hygiene and safety of the factory." Its intention is in line with the 20th recommendation of the Fifth International Labour Conference regarding factory inspection. In recent decades, the task of factory inspectors has increasingly focused on cooperating with labor and management to improve the conditions of factories and workers, rather than focusing solely on investigation and punishment. The history of factory inspections in various countries proves that the reduction of violations does not lie in the severity of punishment, but in whether the inspector can cooperate with both labor and management to prevent problems before they occur. Therefore, factory owners in various countries have recently changed their previous suspicious and disgusted attitude towards inspectors and have come to regard inspectors as mentors and good friends for improving factory equipment. Now, when our country's factory management is urgently seeking improvement, this external assistance should not be ignored.

Incoming Letter

Respected Editor, I recently saw a section in your newspaper's local news column on the 25th of this month about a conflict between the comprador and tea servers of the Chang'an steamer. The details stated therein do not conform to the facts. Now I will describe the details of what happened and request that you make corrections. Upon investigation, when the Chang'an steamer arrived in Hankou, it happened to be the Lunar New Year. When it departed from Shanghai, the comprador Xiangqing notified all the tea servers that the Lunar New Year had been abolished this year. According to the company's orders, all personnel in all departments were to cancel the New Year celebration. However, the ship's crew members and the comprador's tallymen all contributed money to celebrate the New Year on their own. The tea servers mistakenly thought that the crew members and tallymen were all celebrating the festival, but the tea servers alone were not. They did not know the details and made rude remarks, scolding the comprador severely. After mediation by various staff members proved ineffective, the tea server leader, Zhuo Cixu, physically attacked the comprador. Seeing the menacing situation, Xiangqing fled to the main kitchen to avoid being hit. Zhao Shichun fell into the water after slipping on the snow while chasing the comprador, but was rescued immediately. When the conflict occurred, six tea servers had minor skin injuries, but were not seriously injured. As for Ren Jinding's death, the Hankou court confirmed that he died of illness. Currently, this case is awaiting investigation and judgment by the Hankou court. The information published in your newspaper is not accurate, so I am sending this special letter to request corrections to avoid causing disputes. I would be grateful. Respectfully yours, Li Xiangqing, comprador of the Chang'an Steamer, February 26th.
